api documentation for errors (v0.3.0)

A comprehensive, robust, yet lightweight set of error utilities for node.js enabling you to do errors more effectively.

module errors

function errors.Http400Error (msg, expl, fix)

  • description and source-code
    Http400Error = function (msg, expl, fix) {
	var attrs = {};
	if (typeof msg !== null && typeof msg === 'object') {
		attrs = msg;
		msg = attrs['message'] || defaultMessage;
		if (attrs.hasOwnProperty('stack')
				|| attrs.hasOwnProperty('name')
				|| attrs.hasOwnProperty('code')) {
			throw Error("Properties 'stack', 'name' or 'code' " +
					"cannot be overridden");
		}
	}
	attrs['status'] = attrs['status'] || statusCode;
    msg = msg || defaultMessage;
    expl = expl || defaultExplanation;
    fix = fix || defaultResponse;

    parent.call(this, msg);

    // hack around the defineProperty for stack so
    // we can delay stack formatting until access
    // for performance reasons
    Error.captureStackTrace(stack, scope[className]);

/**
 * Return the stack tracks for the error.
 *
 * @return {String}
 * @api public
 */
    Object.defineProperty(this, 'stack', {
        configurable: true,
        enumerable: false,
        get: function() {
            if (!formattedStack) {
                formattedStack = stack.stack.replace('[object Object]', 'Error: ' + this.message);
            }
            return formattedStack;
        }
    });

/**
 * Return the explanation for this error.
 *
 * @return {String}
 * @api public
*/

    Object.defineProperty(this, 'explanation', {
        value: attrs['explanation'] || expl,
        configurable: true,
        enumerable: true
    });

/**
 * Return the operator response for this error.
 *
 * @return {String}
 * @api public
 */

    Object.defineProperty(this, 'response', {
        value: attrs['response'] || fix,
        configurable: true,
        enumerable: true
    });

/**
 * Return the error code.
 *
 * @return {Number}
 * @api public
 */

    Object.defineProperty(this, 'code', {
        value: attrs['code'] || errorCode,
        configurable: true,
        enumerable: true
    });

/**
 * HTTP status code of this error.
 *
 * If the instance's `code` is not a valid
 * HTTP status code it's normalized to 500.s
 *
 * @return {Number}
 * @api public
 */

    Object.defineProperty(this, 'status', {
        value: attrs['status'] || (http.STATUS_CODES[errorCode] ? errorCode : 500),
        configurable: true,
        // normalize for http status code and connect compat
        enumerable: true
    });

/**
 * Name of this error.
 *
 * @return {String}
 * @api public
 */

    Object.defineProperty(this, 'name', {
        value: className,
        configurable: true,
        enumerable: true
    });

/**
 * Message for this error.
 *
 * @return {String}
 * @api public
 */

    Object.defineProperty(this, 'message', {
        value: attrs['message'] || msg,
        configurable: true,
        enumerable: true
    });

    // expose extra conf attrs as properties
    for (var key in attrs) {
		if (!this.hasOwnProperty(key)) {
			Object.defineProperty(this, key, {
	            value: attrs[key],
	            configurable: true,
	            enumerable: true
	        });
		}
	}

}
  • example usage
    ...
errors.mapper('RangeError', function(rangeError) {
    return new errors.Http412Error('Invalid range requested');
})
.mapper('ReferenceError', function(refError) {
    return new errors.Http424Error('Bad reference given');
})
.mapper('SyntaxError', function(syntaxError) {
    return new errors.Http400Error('Invalid syntax');
});

// ...

res.send(new RangeError());
// => 412 response as per mapper
...

    Object.defineProperty(this, 'status', {
        value: attrs['status'] || (http.STATUS_CODES[errorCode] ? errorCode : 500),
        configurable: true,
        // normalize for http status code and connect compat
        enumerable: true
    });

 * @return {String}
 * @api public
 */

    Object.defineProperty(this, 'name', {
        value: className,
        configurable: true,
        enumerable: true
    });

/**

 *
 * @return {String}
 * @api public

    Object.defineProperty(this, 'message', {
        value: attrs['message'] || msg,
        configurable: true,
        enumerable: true
    });

    // expose extra conf attrs as properties
    for (var key in attrs) {
		if (!this.hasOwnProperty(key)) {
			Object.defineProperty(this, key, {

	            configurable: true,
	            enumerable: true
	        });
		}

Explanation: You do not have access to read /root/foo
Response: Request a file you have permissions to access

```

Use the options style constructor to assign standard properties:
```js
console.log(new errors.Http401Error({
	message: "Expired Token",
	explanation: "Your token has expired"}).toString());
```

outputs:
```
Http401Error: Expired Token

function errors.Http402Error (msg, expl, fix)

  • description and source-code
    Http402Error = function (msg, expl, fix) {
	var attrs = {};
	if (typeof msg !== null && typeof msg === 'object') {
		attrs = msg;
		msg = attrs['message'] || defaultMessage;
		if (attrs.hasOwnProperty('stack')
				|| attrs.hasOwnProperty('name')
				|| attrs.hasOwnProperty('code')) {
			throw Error("Properties 'stack', 'name' or 'code' " +
					"cannot be overridden");
		}
	}
	attrs['status'] = attrs['status'] || statusCode;
    msg = msg || defaultMessage;
    expl = expl || defaultExplanation;
    fix = fix || defaultResponse;

    parent.call(this, msg);

    // hack around the defineProperty for stack so
    // we can delay stack formatting until access
    // for performance reasons
    Error.captureStackTrace(stack, scope[className]);

/**
 * Return the stack tracks for the error.
 *
 * @return {String}
 * @api public
 */
    Object.defineProperty(this, 'stack', {
        configurable: true,
        enumerable: false,
        get: function() {
            if (!formattedStack) {
                formattedStack = stack.stack.replace('[object Object]', 'Error: ' + this.message);
            }
            return formattedStack;
        }
    });

/**
 * Return the explanation for this error.
 *
 * @return {String}
 * @api public
*/

    Object.defineProperty(this, 'explanation', {
        value: attrs['explanation'] || expl,
        configurable: true,
        enumerable: true
    });

 * Return the operator response for this error.
 *
 * @return {String}
 * @api public
 */

        value: attrs['response'] || fix,
        configurable: true,
        enumerable: true
    });

/**
 * Return the error code.
 *
 * @return {Number}
 * @api public
 */

    Object.defineProperty(this, 'code', {
        value: attrs['code'] || errorCode,
        configurable: true,
        enumerable: true
    });

/**
 * HTTP status code of this error.
 *
 * If the instance's `code` is not a valid
 * HTTP status code it's normalized to 500.s
 *
 * @return {Number}
 * @api public
 */

    Object.defineProperty(this, 'status', {
        value: attrs['status'] || (http.STATUS_CODES[errorCode] ? errorCode : 500),
        configurable: true,
        // normalize for http status code and connect compat
        enumerable: true
    });

 * Name of this error.

  • example usage
    ...
installed. If express is installed, errors automatically patches `express`'s
`response.send()` method to support `send()`ing `Error` based objects.

So the following is valid:
```js
app.get('/users/:user', function(req, res) {
    users.get(req.params.user, function(err, user) {
        return res.send(err || user || new errors.Http404Error('User does not exist
'));
    });
});
```

By default both vanilla errors (those provided by the JS runtime) and errors
which have a `code` which is not a valid HTTP status code are mapped to a `500`
response.
...

        get: function() {
            if (!formattedStack) {
                formattedStack = stack.stack.replace('[object Object]', 'Error: ' + this.message);
            }
            return formattedStack;
        }
    });

/**
 * Return the explanation for this error.
 *
 * @return {String}
 * @api public
*/

    Object.defineProperty(this, 'explanation', {
        value: attrs['explanation'] || expl,
        configurable: true,
        enumerable: true
    });

/**
 * Return the operator response for this error.
 *
 * @return {String}
 * @api public
 */

    Object.defineProperty(this, 'response', {
        value: attrs['response'] || fix,
        configurable: true,
        enumerable: true
    });

/**
 * Return the error code.
 *
 * @return {Number}
 * @api public
 */

    Object.defineProperty(this, 'code', {
        value: attrs['code'] || errorCode,
        configurable: true,
        enumerable: true
    });

/**
 * HTTP status code of this error.
 *
 * If the instance's `code` is not a valid
 * HTTP status code it's normalized to 500.s
 *
 * @return {Number}
 * @api public
 */

    Object.defineProperty(this, 'status', {
        value: attrs['status'] || (http.STATUS_CODES[errorCode] ? errorCode : 500),
        configurable: true,
        // normalize for http status code and connect compat
        enumerable: true
    });

/**
 * Name of this error.
 *
 * @return {String}
 * @api public
 */

    Object.defineProperty(this, 'name', {
        value: className,
        configurable: true,
        enumerable: true
    });

/**
 * Message for this error.
 *
 * @return {String}
 * @api public
 */

    Object.defineProperty(this, 'message', {
        value: attrs['message'] || msg,
        configurable: true,
        enumerable: true
    });

    // expose extra conf attrs as properties
    for (var key in attrs) {
		if (!this.hasOwnProperty(key)) {
			Object.defineProperty(this, key, {
	            value: attrs[key],
	            configurable: true,
	            enumerable: true
	        });
		}
	}

}

both will result in a `500` response.

Mappers can also be used with `express`'s `send()` method.

For example:
```js
errors.mapper('RangeError', function(rangeError) {
    return new errors.Http412Error('Invalid range requested');
})
.mapper('ReferenceError', function(refError) {
    return new errors.Http424Error('Bad reference given');
})
.mapper('SyntaxError', function(syntaxError) {
    return new errors.Http400Error('Invalid syntax');
});

  • example usage
    ...
like `toString()` and `toJSON()` return representation without stack
traces. You can enable stack traces by leveraging the `errors.stacks()`
method.

For example:
```js
errors.stacks(true);
new errors.Http413Error().toString();
// => includes stack trace
new errors.Http413Error().toJSON();
// => includes a 'stack' property
```

You can also use the `errors.stacks()` method without arguments to
retrieve the current value of stacks.
...

```js
errors.mapper('RangeError', function(rangeError) {
    return new errors.Http412Error('Invalid range requested');
})
.mapper('ReferenceError', function(refError) {
    return new errors.Http424Error('Bad reference given');
})
.mapper('SyntaxError', function(syntaxError) {
    return new errors.Http400Error('Invalid syntax');
});

  • example usage
    ...
naming convention `Http[code]Error`. For example `Http401Error` and
`Http500Error` which have a code of `401` and `500` respectively.

For example to leverage the HTTP errors:
```js
throw new errors.Http401Error();
// ...
throw new errors.Http500Error('Something bad happened');
```

## Connect/Express middleware integration

**Compatibility**
Errors version 0.1.0 only works with Express < 4.0.0.
...

        enumerable: true
    });

/**
 * Return the operator response for this error.
 *
 * @return {String}
 * @api public
 */

    Object.defineProperty(this, 'response', {
        value: attrs['response'] || fix,
        configurable: true,
        enumerable: true
    });

/**
 * Return the error code.
 *
 * @return {Number}
 * @api public
 */

    Object.defineProperty(this, 'code', {
        value: attrs['code'] || errorCode,
        configurable: true,
        enumerable: true
    });

/**
 * HTTP status code of this error.
 *
 * If the instance's `code` is not a valid
 * HTTP status code it's normalized to 500.s
 *
 * @return {Number}
 * @api public
 */

    Object.defineProperty(this, 'status', {
        value: attrs['status'] || (http.STATUS_CODES[errorCode] ? errorCode : 500),
        configurable: true,
        // normalize for http status code and connect compat
        enumerable: true
    });

/**
 * Name of this error.
 *
 * @return {String}
 * @api public
 */

    Object.defineProperty(this, 'name', {
        value: className,
        configurable: true,
        enumerable: true
    });

/**
 * Message for this error.
 *
 * @return {String}
 * @api public
 */

    Object.defineProperty(this, 'message', {
        value: attrs['message'] || msg,
        configurable: true,
        enumerable: true
    });

    // expose extra conf attrs as properties
    for (var key in attrs) {
		if (!this.hasOwnProperty(key)) {
			Object.defineProperty(this, key, {
	            value: attrs[key],
	            configurable: true,
	            enumerable: true
	        });
		}
	}

}

function errors.create (options)

  • description and source-code
    create = function (options) {
    var options = options || {}
        , scope = options.scope || exports
        , parent = options.parent || Error
        , defaultMessage = options.defaultMessage
            || 'An unexpected ' + options.name + ' occurred.'
        , className = options.name
        , errorCode = options.code || nextCode()
        , statusCode = options.status
        , defaultExplanation = options.defaultExplanation
        , defaultResponse = options.defaultResponse
        , formattedStack
        , stack = {};


/**
 * Create a new instance of the exception which accepts
 * 2 forms of parameters.
 *
 * (a) Passing the message, explanation and response
 * as individual argument strings:
 * Create a new instance of the exception optionally
 * specifying a message, explanation and response
 * for the new instance. If any of the arguments are
 * null, their value will default to their respective
 * default value use on the `create` call, or will
 * be null if no default was specified.
 *
 * (b) Passing an options style object which contains
 * key / value pairs. In this form keys map to the
 * attributes of the error object. Note that the properties
 * 'stack', 'name' and 'code' cannot be set via the options
 * style object in this form.
 *
 * @param {String|Object} msg The message to use for the error.
 * @param {String} expl The explanation to use for the error.
 * @param {String} fix The response to use for the error.
 * @return {Object} The newly created error.
 */

    scope[className] = function(msg, expl, fix) {
    	var attrs = {};
    	if (typeof msg !== null && typeof msg === 'object') {
    		attrs = msg;
    		msg = attrs['message'] || defaultMessage;
    		if (attrs.hasOwnProperty('stack')
    				|| attrs.hasOwnProperty('name')
    				|| attrs.hasOwnProperty('code')) {
    			throw Error("Properties 'stack', 'name' or 'code' " +
    					"cannot be overridden");
    		}
    	}
    	attrs['status'] = attrs['status'] || statusCode;
        msg = msg || defaultMessage;
        expl = expl || defaultExplanation;
        fix = fix || defaultResponse;

        parent.call(this, msg);

        // hack around the defineProperty for stack so
        // we can delay stack formatting until access
        // for performance reasons
        Error.captureStackTrace(stack, scope[className]);

/**
 * Return the stack tracks for the error.
 *
 * @return {String}
 * @api public
 */
        Object.defineProperty(this, 'stack', {
            configurable: true,
            enumerable: false,
            get: function() {
                if (!formattedStack) {
                    formattedStack = stack.stack.replace('[object Object]', 'Error: ' + this.message);
                }
                return formattedStack;
            }
        });

/**
 * Return the explanation for this error.
 *
 * @return {String}
 * @api public
*/

        Object.defineProperty(this, 'explanation', {
            value: attrs['explanation'] || expl,
            configurable: true,
            enumerable: true
        });

/**
 * Return the operator response for this error.
 *
 * @return {String}
 * @api public
 */

        Object.defineProperty(this, 'response', {
            value: attrs['response'] || fix,
            configurable: true,
            enumerable: true
        });

/**
 * Return the error code.
 *
 * @return {Number}
 * @api public
 */

        Object.defineProperty(this, 'code', {
            value: attrs['code'] || errorCode,
            configurable: true,
            enumerable: true
        });

/**
 * HTTP status code of this error.
 *
 * If the instance's `code` is not a valid
 * HTTP status code it's normalized to 500.s
 *
 * @return {Number}
 * @api public
 */

        Object.defineProperty(this, 'status', {
            value: attrs['status'] || (http.STATUS_CODES[errorCode] ? errorCode : 500),
            configurable: true,
            // normalize for http status code and connect compat
            enumerable: true
        });

/**
 * Name of this error.
 *
 * @return {String}
 * @api public
 */

        Obje ...

require('errors');
```

Create a very barebones error -- you must specify at least the error name:

```js
// barebones
errors.create({name: 'RuntimeError'});
console.log(new errors.RuntimeError().toString());
```

produces:
```
RuntimeError: An unexpected RuntimeError occurred.
Code: 601

function errors.errorToJSON (err, attrMap)

  • description and source-code
    errorToJSON = function (err, attrMap) {
	var attrs = attrMap || _DEFAULT_ERROR_MAPPING,
		formatted = {};

	for (var dest in attrs) {
		for (var attr_index in attrs[dest]) {
			var val = err,
				src = attrs[dest][attr_index],
				segs = src.split('.');
			for (var seg_index in segs) {
				if (segs[seg_index] == 'stack' && !useStack) {
					val = null;
					break;
				}
				val = segs[seg_index] in val ? val[segs[seg_index]] : null;
			}
			if (val != null) {
				formatted[dest] = val;
			}
		}
	}
	return formatted;
}
  • example usage
    ...
```

## Native errors

Often times you need to extract 'errors-like' properties from native error
objects. For example you have a native JS or node error and you want to
extract it's errors-like properties. An error's module-level function
called `errors.errorToJSON()` allows you to do this.

For example to extract error properties from a native error (`errors.stacks`
is set to `false` in this example):
```js
console.log("%j", errors.errorToJSON(new TypeError("Bad type")));
```
...

function errors.find (err)

  • description and source-code
    find = function (err) {
    return (typeof err == 'number') ? codes[err] : names[err];
}
  • example usage
    ...

For convenience, errors keeps track of all the errors you've defined
via the errors module and allows you to look them up via `name` or
`code`.

So from our previous example:
```js
errors.find(1100);
errors.find('SecurityError')
```

Will both return the `SecutiryError` we defined.

function errors.mapError (err)

  • description and source-code
    mapError = function (err) {
    return mapper(err.name) ? mapper(err.name)(err) : err;
}
  • example usage
    ...
```js
// mappers
errors.create({name: 'InvalidUsernameError'});
errors.create({name: 'InvalidPasswordError'});
errors.mapper(['InvalidUsernameError', 'InvalidPasswordError'], function(err) {
    return new errors.SecurityError('Invalid credentials supplied');
});
console.log(errors.mapError(new errors.InvalidUsernameError()).toString());
console.log(errors.mapError(new errors.InvalidPasswordError()).toString());
```

outputs:
```
SecurityError: Invalid credentials supplied
Code: 1100
...

function errors.mapper (errName, fn)

  • description and source-code
    mapper = function (errName, fn) {
    if (arguments.length == 2) {
        asArray(errName).forEach(function(name) {
            mappers[name] = fn;
        });
        return exports;
    }
    return mappers[errName];
}
  • example usage
    ...

For example if you wanted to mask invalid user and password errors into
a generic credentials error:
```js
// mappers
errors.create({name: 'InvalidUsernameError'});
errors.create({name: 'InvalidPasswordError'});
errors.mapper(['InvalidUsernameError', 'InvalidPasswordError'], function
(err) {
    return new errors.SecurityError('Invalid credentials supplied');
});
console.log(errors.mapError(new errors.InvalidUsernameError()).toString());
console.log(errors.mapError(new errors.InvalidPasswordError()).toString());
```

outputs:
...

function errors.stacks (useStacks)

  • description and source-code
    stacks = function (useStacks) {
    if (useStacks == null || useStacks == undefined) {
        return useStack;
    }
    useStack = useStacks;
}
  • example usage
    ...

Will both return the `SecutiryError` we defined.

## Stack traces

By default stack traces are disabled which means that error methods
like `toString()` and `toJSON()` return representation without stack
traces. You can enable stack traces by leveraging the `errors.stacks()`
method.

For example:
```js
errors.stacks(true);
new errors.Http413Error().toString();
// => includes stack trace
...

function errors.title (title)

  • description and source-code
    title = function (title) {
    if (title == null || title == undefined) {
        return pageTitle;
    }
    pageTitle = title;
}
  • example usage
    ...
    "message": "An unexpected DatabaseConnectionError occurred."
}
```

For HTML based responses, `send()`ing an error will produce a HTML
response that looks like express's or connect's `errorHandler()` middleware.
That is, it's an HTML page with minimal styling. Moreover you can control
the HTML response page title using the `errors.title('My Title')` method.
You can also control if stack traces should be included in the `send()` by
using the `errors.stacks()` method.

function errors.Http400Error.prototype.toString ()

  • description and source-code
    toString = function () {

    /*!

    The snippet below would allow us to provide connect errorHandler()
    middleware compatible errors, but is too costly. In a 1000 executions
    of toString() it adds ~25% overhead.

    var e = Error();
    Error.captureStackTrace(e);
    if (~e.stack.indexOf("connect/lib/middleware/errorHandler.js")) {
        return this.message;
    }
    */

    // TODO externalization
    var msg = util.format("%s: %s\nCode: %s", this.name, this.message, this.code);
    if (this.explanation) {
        msg += "\nExplanation: " + this.explanation;
    }
    if (this.response) {
        msg += "\nResponse: " + this.response;
    }

    function isExtra(key) {
    	return ['name', 'message', 'status', 'code',
    	        'response', 'explanation', 'stack'].indexOf(key) < 0;
    }

    // extra properties
    Object.keys(this).filter(isExtra).forEach(function(key) {
    	msg += util.format("\n%s: %s", key, this[key]);
    }, this);

    if (useStack) {
        msg += "\n" + this.stack;
    }
    return msg;
}
  • example usage
    ...
```

 * Name of this error.
 *
 * @return {String}
 * @api public
 */

    Object.defineProperty(this, 'name', {
        value: className,
        configurable: true,
        enumerable: true
    });

/**
 * Message for this error.
 *
 * @return {String}
 * @api public
 */

    Object.defineProperty(this, 'message', {
        value: attrs['message'] || msg,
        configurable: true,
        enumerable: true
    });

    // expose extra conf attrs as properties
    for (var key in attrs) {
		if (!this.hasOwnProperty(key)) {
			Object.defineProperty(this, key, {
	            value: attrs[key],
	            configurable: true,
	            enumerable: true
	        });
		}
	}

}
  • example usage
    ...
Explanation: You do not have access to read /root/foo
Response: Request a file you have permissions to access

```

Use the options style constructor to assign standard properties:
```js
console.log(new errors.Http401Error({
	message: "Expired Token",
	explanation: "Your token has expired"}).toString());
```

outputs:
```
Http401Error: Expired Token

function errors.Http401Error.super_ (msg, expl, fix)

  • description and source-code
    super_ = function (msg, expl, fix) {
	var attrs = {};
	if (typeof msg !== null && typeof msg === 'object') {
		attrs = msg;
		msg = attrs['message'] || defaultMessage;
		if (attrs.hasOwnProperty('stack')
				|| attrs.hasOwnProperty('name')
				|| attrs.hasOwnProperty('code')) {
			throw Error("Properties 'stack', 'name' or 'code' " +
					"cannot be overridden");
		}
	}
	attrs['status'] = attrs['status'] || statusCode;
    msg = msg || defaultMessage;
    expl = expl || defaultExplanation;
    fix = fix || defaultResponse;

    parent.call(this, msg);

    // hack around the defineProperty for stack so
    // we can delay stack formatting until access
    // for performance reasons
    Error.captureStackTrace(stack, scope[className]);

/**
 * Return the stack tracks for the error.
 *
 * @return {String}
 * @api public
 */
    Object.defineProperty(this, 'stack', {
        configurable: true,
        enumerable: false,
        get: function() {
            if (!formattedStack) {
                formattedStack = stack.stack.replace('[object Object]', 'Error: ' + this.message);
            }
            return formattedStack;
        }
    });

/**
 * Return the explanation for this error.
 *
 * @return {String}
 * @api public
*/

    Object.defineProperty(this, 'explanation', {
        value: attrs['explanation'] || expl,
        configurable: true,
        enumerable: true
    });

/**
 * Return the operator response for this error.
 *
 * @return {String}
 * @api public
 */

    Object.defineProperty(this, 'response', {
        value: attrs['response'] || fix,
        configurable: true,
        enumerable: true
    });

/**
 * Return the error code.
 *
 * @return {Number}
 * @api public
 */

    Object.defineProperty(this, 'code', {
        value: attrs['code'] || errorCode,
        configurable: true,
        enumerable: true
    });

/**
 * HTTP status code of this error.
 *
 * If the instance's `code` is not a valid
 * HTTP status code it's normalized to 500.s
 *
 * @return {Number}
 * @api public
 */

    Object.defineProperty(this, 'status', {
        value: attrs['status'] || (http.STATUS_CODES[errorCode] ? errorCode : 500),
        configurable: true,
        // normalize for http status code and connect compat
        enumerable: true
    });

/**
 * Name of this error.
 *
 * @return {String}
 * @api public
 */

    Object.defineProperty(this, 'name', {
        value: className,
        configurable: true,
        enumerable: true
    });

/**
 * Message for this error.
 *
 * @return {String}
 * @api public
 */

    Object.defineProperty(this, 'message', {
        value: attrs['message'] || msg,
        configurable: true,
        enumerable: true
    });

    // expose extra conf attrs as properties
    for (var key in attrs) {
		if (!this.hasOwnProperty(key)) {
			Object.defineProperty(this, key, {
	            value: attrs[key],
	            configurable: true,
	            enumerable: true
	        });
		}
	}

}

module errors.Http401Error.prototype

function errors.Http401Error.prototype.toJSON ()

    // TODO externalization
    return useStack
            ? mixin(this, {stack: this.stack}, true)
            : mixin(this, {}, true);
}
  • example usage
    ...
method.

For example:
```js
errors.stacks(true);
new errors.Http413Error().toString();
// => includes stack trace
new errors.Http413Error().toJSON();
// => includes a 'stack' property
```

You can also use the `errors.stacks()` method without arguments to
retrieve the current value of stacks.

This allows you to write code like:
...

function errors.Http401Error.prototype.toString ()

  • description and source-code
    toString = function () {

    /*!

    The snippet below would allow us to provide connect errorHandler()
    middleware compatible errors, but is too costly. In a 1000 executions
    of toString() it adds ~25% overhead.

    var e = Error();
    Error.captureStackTrace(e);
    if (~e.stack.indexOf("connect/lib/middleware/errorHandler.js")) {
        return this.message;
    }
    */

    // TODO externalization
    var msg = util.format("%s: %s\nCode: %s", this.name, this.message, this.code);
    if (this.explanation) {
        msg += "\nExplanation: " + this.explanation;
    }
    if (this.response) {
        msg += "\nResponse: " + this.response;
    }

    function isExtra(key) {
    	return ['name', 'message', 'status', 'code',
    	        'response', 'explanation', 'stack'].indexOf(key) < 0;
    }

    // extra properties
    Object.keys(this).filter(isExtra).forEach(function(key) {
    	msg += util.format("\n%s: %s", key, this[key]);
    }, this);

    if (useStack) {
        msg += "\n" + this.stack;
    }
    return msg;
}
  • example usage
    ...
```

Create a very barebones error -- you must specify at least the error name:

```js
// barebones
errors.create({name: 'RuntimeError'});
console.log(new errors.RuntimeError().toString());
```

produces:
```
RuntimeError: An unexpected RuntimeError occurred.
Code: 601
```

    });

/**
 * Return the error code.
 *
 * @return {Number}
 * @api public
 */

    Object.defineProperty(this, 'code', {
        value: attrs['code'] || errorCode,
        configurable: true,
        enumerable: true
    });

/**
 * HTTP status code of this error.
 *
 * If the instance's `code` is not a valid
 * HTTP status code it's normalized to 500.s
 *
 * @return {Number}
 * @api public
 */

    Object.defineProperty(this, 'status', {
        value: attrs['status'] || (http.STATUS_CODES[errorCode] ? errorCode : 500),
        configurable: true,
        // normalize for http status code and connect compat
        enumerable: true
    });

/**
 * Name of this error.
 *
 * @return {String}
 * @api public
 */

    Object.defineProperty(this, 'name', {
        value: className,
        configurable: true,
        enumerable: true
    });

/**
 * Message for this error.
 *
 * @return {String}
 * @api public
 */

    Object.defineProperty(this, 'message', {
        value: attrs['message'] || msg,
        configurable: true,
        enumerable: true
    });

    // expose extra conf attrs as properties
    for (var key in attrs) {
		if (!this.hasOwnProperty(key)) {
			Object.defineProperty(this, key, {
	            value: attrs[key],
	            configurable: true,
	            enumerable: true
	        });
		}
	}

}
  • example usage
    ...
installed. If express is installed, errors automatically patches `express`'s
`response.send()` method to support `send()`ing `Error` based objects.

So the following is valid:
```js
app.get('/users/:user', function(req, res) {
    users.get(req.params.user, function(err, user) {
        return res.send(err || user || new errors.Http404Error('User does not exist
'));
    });
});
```

By default both vanilla errors (those provided by the JS runtime) and errors
which have a `code` which is not a valid HTTP status code are mapped to a `500`
response.
...

module errors.Http404Error.prototype

function errors.Http404Error.prototype.toJSON ()

  • description and source-code
    toJSON = function () {
    // TODO externalization
    return useStack
            ? mixin(this, {stack: this.stack}, true)
            : mixin(this, {}, true);
}
  • example usage
    ...
method.

For example:
```js
errors.stacks(true);
new errors.Http413Error().toString();
// => includes stack trace
new errors.Http413Error().toJSON();
// => includes a 'stack' property
```

You can also use the `errors.stacks()` method without arguments to
retrieve the current value of stacks.

This allows you to write code like:
...

function errors.Http404Error.prototype.toString ()

  • description and source-code
    toString = function () {

    /*!

    The snippet below would allow us to provide connect errorHandler()
    middleware compatible errors, but is too costly. In a 1000 executions
    of toString() it adds ~25% overhead.

    var e = Error();
    Error.captureStackTrace(e);
    if (~e.stack.indexOf("connect/lib/middleware/errorHandler.js")) {
        return this.message;
    }
    */

    // TODO externalization
    var msg = util.format("%s: %s\nCode: %s", this.name, this.message, this.code);
    if (this.explanation) {
        msg += "\nExplanation: " + this.explanation;
    }
    if (this.response) {
        msg += "\nResponse: " + this.response;
    }

    function isExtra(key) {
    	return ['name', 'message', 'status', 'code',
    	        'response', 'explanation', 'stack'].indexOf(key) < 0;
    }

    // extra properties
    Object.keys(this).filter(isExtra).forEach(function(key) {
    	msg += util.format("\n%s: %s", key, this[key]);
    }, this);

    if (useStack) {
        msg += "\n" + this.stack;
    }
    return msg;
}
  • example usage
    ...
```

Create a very barebones error -- you must specify at least the error name:

```js
// barebones
errors.create({name: 'RuntimeError'});
console.log(new errors.RuntimeError().toString());
```

produces:
```
RuntimeError: An unexpected RuntimeError occurred.
Code: 601
```

    Error.captureStackTrace(stack, scope[className]);

/**
 * Return the stack tracks for the error.
 *
 * @return {String}
 * @api public
 */
    Object.defineProperty(this, 'stack', {
        configurable: true,
        enumerable: false,
        get: function() {
            if (!formattedStack) {
                formattedStack = stack.stack.replace('[object Object]', 'Error: ' + this.message);
            }
            return formattedStack;
        }
    });

/**
 * Return the explanation for this error.
 *
 * @return {String}
 * @api public
*/

    Object.defineProperty(this, 'explanation', {
        value: attrs['explanation'] || expl,
        configurable: true,
        enumerable: true
    });

/**
 * Return the operator response for this error.
 *
 * @return {String}
 * @api public
 */

    Object.defineProperty(this, 'response', {
        value: attrs['response'] || fix,
        configurable: true,
        enumerable: true
    });

/**
 * Return the error code.
 *
 * @return {Number}
 * @api public
 */

    Object.defineProperty(this, 'code', {
        value: attrs['code'] || errorCode,
        configurable: true,
        enumerable: true
    });

/**
 * HTTP status code of this error.
 *
 * If the instance's `code` is not a valid
 * HTTP status code it's normalized to 500.s
 *
 * @return {Number}
 * @api public
 */

    Object.defineProperty(this, 'status', {
        value: attrs['status'] || (http.STATUS_CODES[errorCode] ? errorCode : 500),
        configurable: true,
        // normalize for http status code and connect compat
        enumerable: true
    });

/**
 * Name of this error.
 *
 * @return {String}
 * @api public
 */

    Object.defineProperty(this, 'name', {
        value: className,
        configurable: true,
        enumerable: true
    });

/**
 * Message for this error.
 *
 * @return {String}
 * @api public
 */

    Object.defineProperty(this, 'message', {
        value: attrs['message'] || msg,
        configurable: true,
        enumerable: true
    });

    // expose extra conf attrs as properties
    for (var key in attrs) {
		if (!this.hasOwnProperty(key)) {
			Object.defineProperty(this, key, {
	            value: attrs[key],
	            configurable: true,
	            enumerable: true
	        });
		}
	}

}

module errors.Http407Error.prototype

function errors.Http407Error.prototype.toJSON ()

  • description and source-code
    toJSON = function () {
    // TODO externalization
    return useStack
            ? mixin(this, {stack: this.stack}, true)
            : mixin(this, {}, true);
}
  • example usage
    ...
method.

For example:
```js
errors.stacks(true);
new errors.Http413Error().toString();
// => includes stack trace
new errors.Http413Error().toJSON();
// => includes a 'stack' property
```

You can also use the `errors.stacks()` method without arguments to
retrieve the current value of stacks.

This allows you to write code like:
...

function errors.Http407Error.prototype.toString ()

  • description and source-code
    toString = function () {

    /*!

    The snippet below would allow us to provide connect errorHandler()
    middleware compatible errors, but is too costly. In a 1000 executions
    of toString() it adds ~25% overhead.

    var e = Error();
    Error.captureStackTrace(e);
    if (~e.stack.indexOf("connect/lib/middleware/errorHandler.js")) {
        return this.message;
    }
    */

    // TODO externalization
    var msg = util.format("%s: %s\nCode: %s", this.name, this.message, this.code);
    if (this.explanation) {
        msg += "\nExplanation: " + this.explanation;
    }
    if (this.response) {
        msg += "\nResponse: " + this.response;
    }

    function isExtra(key) {
    	return ['name', 'message', 'status', 'code',
    	        'response', 'explanation', 'stack'].indexOf(key) < 0;
    }

    // extra properties
    Object.keys(this).filter(isExtra).forEach(function(key) {
    	msg += util.format("\n%s: %s", key, this[key]);
    }, this);

    if (useStack) {
        msg += "\n" + this.stack;
    }
    return msg;
}
  • example usage
    ...
```

Create a very barebones error -- you must specify at least the error name:

```js
// barebones
errors.create({name: 'RuntimeError'});
console.log(new errors.RuntimeError().toString());
```

produces:
```
RuntimeError: An unexpected RuntimeError occurred.
Code: 601
```
...

				|| attrs.hasOwnProperty('code')) {
			throw Error("Properties 'stack', 'name' or 'code' " +
					"cannot be overridden");
		}
	}
	attrs['status'] = attrs['status'] || statusCode;
    msg = msg || defaultMessage;
    expl = expl || defaultExplanation;
    fix = fix || defaultResponse;

    parent.call(this, msg);

    // hack around the defineProperty for stack so
    // we can delay stack formatting until access
    // for performance reasons
    Error.captureStackTrace(stack, scope[className]);

/**
 * Return the stack tracks for the error.
 *
 * @return {String}
 * @api public
 */
    Object.defineProperty(this, 'stack', {
        configurable: true,
        enumerable: false,
        get: function() {
            if (!formattedStack) {
                formattedStack = stack.stack.replace('[object Object]', 'Error: ' + this.message);
            }
            return formattedStack;
        }
    });

/**
 * Return the explanation for this error.
 *
 * @return {String}
 * @api public
*/

    Object.defineProperty(this, 'explanation', {
        value: attrs['explanation'] || expl,
        configurable: true,
        enumerable: true
    });

/**
 * Return the operator response for this error.
 *
 * @return {String}
 * @api public
 */

    Object.defineProperty(this, 'response', {
        value: attrs['response'] || fix,
        configurable: true,
        enumerable: true
    });

/**
 * Return the error code.
 *
 * @return {Number}
 * @api public
 */

    Object.defineProperty(this, 'code', {
        value: attrs['code'] || errorCode,
        configurable: true,
        enumerable: true
    });

/**
 * HTTP status code of this error.
 *
 * If the instance's `code` is not a valid
 * HTTP status code it's normalized to 500.s
 *
 * @return {Number}
 * @api public
 */

    Object.defineProperty(this, 'status', {
        value: attrs['status'] || (http.STATUS_CODES[errorCode] ? errorCode : 500),
        configurable: true,
        // normalize for http status code and connect compat
        enumerable: true
    });

/**
 * Name of this error.
 *
 * @return {String}
 * @api public
 */

    Object.defineProperty(this, 'name', {
        value: className,
        configurable: true,
        enumerable: true
    });

/**
 * Message for this error.
 *
 * @return {String}
 * @api public
 */

    Object.defineProperty(this, 'message', {
        value: attrs['message'] || msg,
        configurable: true,
        enumerable: true
    });

    // expose extra conf attrs as properties
    for (var key in attrs) {
		if (!this.hasOwnProperty(key)) {
			Object.defineProperty(this, key, {
	            value: attrs[key],
	            configurable: true,
	            enumerable: true
	        });
		}
	}

}
  • example usage

module errors.Http410Error.prototype

function errors.Http410Error.prototype.toJSON ()

  • description and source-code
    toJSON = function () {
    // TODO externalization
    return useStack
            ? mixin(this, {stack: this.stack}, true)
            : mixin(this, {}, true);
}
  • example usage
    ...
method.

For example:
```js
errors.stacks(true);
new errors.Http413Error().toString();
// => includes stack trace
new errors.Http413Error().toJSON();
// => includes a 'stack' property
```

You can also use the `errors.stacks()` method without arguments to
retrieve the current value of stacks.

This allows you to write code like:
...

function errors.Http410Error.prototype.toString ()

  • description and source-code
    toString = function () {

    /*!

    The snippet below would allow us to provide connect errorHandler()
    middleware compatible errors, but is too costly. In a 1000 executions
    of toString() it adds ~25% overhead.

    var e = Error();
    Error.captureStackTrace(e);
    if (~e.stack.indexOf("connect/lib/middleware/errorHandler.js")) {
        return this.message;
    }
    */

    // TODO externalization
    var msg = util.format("%s: %s\nCode: %s", this.name, this.message, this.code);
    if (this.explanation) {
        msg += "\nExplanation: " + this.explanation;
    }
    if (this.response) {
        msg += "\nResponse: " + this.response;
    }

    function isExtra(key) {
    	return ['name', 'message', 'status', 'code',
    	        'response', 'explanation', 'stack'].indexOf(key) < 0;
    }

    // extra properties
    Object.keys(this).filter(isExtra).forEach(function(key) {
    	msg += util.format("\n%s: %s", key, this[key]);
    }, this);

    if (useStack) {
        msg += "\n" + this.stack;
    }
    return msg;
}
  • example usage
    ...
```

Create a very barebones error -- you must specify at least the error name:

```js
// barebones
errors.create({name: 'RuntimeError'});
console.log(new errors.RuntimeError().toString());
```

produces:
```
RuntimeError: An unexpected RuntimeError occurred.
Code: 601
```
...

both will result in a `500` response.

Mappers can also be used with `express`'s `send()` method.

For example:
```js
errors.mapper('RangeError', function(rangeError) {
    return new errors.Http412Error('Invalid range requested');
})
.mapper('ReferenceError', function(refError) {
    return new errors.Http424Error('Bad reference given');
})
.mapper('SyntaxError', function(syntaxError) {
    return new errors.Http400Error('Invalid syntax');
});
...

    	msg += util.format("\n%s: %s", key, this[key]);
    }, this);

    if (useStack) {
        msg += "\n" + this.stack;
    }
    return msg;
}
  • example usage
    ...
```

Create a very barebones error -- you must specify at least the error name:

```js
// barebones
errors.create({name: 'RuntimeError'});
console.log(new errors.RuntimeError().toString());
```

produces:
```
RuntimeError: An unexpected RuntimeError occurred.
Code: 601
```

module errors.Http413Error

function errors.Http413Error (msg, expl, fix)

  • description and source-code
    Http413Error = function (msg, expl, fix) {
	var attrs = {};
	if (typeof msg !== null && typeof msg === 'object') {
		attrs = msg;
		msg = attrs['message'] || defaultMessage;
		if (attrs.hasOwnProperty('stack')
				|| attrs.hasOwnProperty('name')
				|| attrs.hasOwnProperty('code')) {
			throw Error("Properties 'stack', 'name' or 'code' " +
					"cannot be overridden");
		}
	}
	attrs['status'] = attrs['status'] || statusCode;
    msg = msg || defaultMessage;
    expl = expl || defaultExplanation;
    fix = fix || defaultResponse;

    parent.call(this, msg);

    // hack around the defineProperty for stack so
    // we can delay stack formatting until access
    // for performance reasons
    Error.captureStackTrace(stack, scope[className]);

/**
 * Return the stack tracks for the error.
 *
 * @return {String}
 * @api public
 */
    Object.defineProperty(this, 'stack', {
        configurable: true,
        enumerable: false,
        get: function() {
            if (!formattedStack) {
                formattedStack = stack.stack.replace('[object Object]', 'Error: ' + this.message);
            }
            return formattedStack;
        }
    });

/**
 * Return the explanation for this error.
 *
 * @return {String}
 * @api public
*/

    Object.defineProperty(this, 'explanation', {
        value: attrs['explanation'] || expl,
        configurable: true,
        enumerable: true
    });

/**
 * Return the operator response for this error.
 *
 * @return {String}
 * @api public
 */

    Object.defineProperty(this, 'response', {
        value: attrs['response'] || fix,
        configurable: true,
        enumerable: true
    });

/**
 * Return the error code.
 *
 * @return {Number}
 * @api public
 */

    Object.defineProperty(this, 'code', {
        value: attrs['code'] || errorCode,
        configurable: true,
        enumerable: true
    });

/**
 * HTTP status code of this error.
 *
 * If the instance's `code` is not a valid
 * HTTP status code it's normalized to 500.s
 *
 * @return {Number}
 * @api public
 */

    Object.defineProperty(this, 'status', {
        value: attrs['status'] || (http.STATUS_CODES[errorCode] ? errorCode : 500),
        configurable: true,
        // normalize for http status code and connect compat
        enumerable: true
    });

/**
 * Name of this error.
 *
 * @return {String}
 * @api public
 */

    Object.defineProperty(this, 'name', {
        value: className,
        configurable: true,
        enumerable: true
    });

/**
 * Message for this error.
 *
 * @return {String}
 * @api public
 */

    Object.defineProperty(this, 'message', {
        value: attrs['message'] || msg,
        configurable: true,
        enumerable: true
    });

    // expose extra conf attrs as properties
    for (var key in attrs) {
		if (!this.hasOwnProperty(key)) {
			Object.defineProperty(this, key, {
	            value: attrs[key],
	            configurable: true,
	            enumerable: true
	        });
		}
	}

}
  • example usage
    ...
like `toString()` and `toJSON()` return representation without stack
traces. You can enable stack traces by leveraging the `errors.stacks()`
method.

For example:
```js
errors.stacks(true);
new errors.Http413Error().toString();
// => includes stack trace
new errors.Http413Error().toJSON();
// => includes a 'stack' property
```

You can also use the `errors.stacks()` method without arguments to
retrieve the current value of stacks.
...

// => includes stack trace

// => includes a 'stack' property

function errors.Http413Error.prototype.toString ()

  • description and source-code
    toString = function () {

    /*!

    The snippet below would allow us to provide connect errorHandler()
    middleware compatible errors, but is too costly. In a 1000 executions
    of toString() it adds ~25% overhead.

    var e = Error();
    Error.captureStackTrace(e);
    if (~e.stack.indexOf("connect/lib/middleware/errorHandler.js")) {
        return this.message;
    }
    */

    // TODO externalization
    var msg = util.format("%s: %s\nCode: %s", this.name, this.message, this.code);
    if (this.explanation) {
        msg += "\nExplanation: " + this.explanation;
    }
    if (this.response) {
        msg += "\nResponse: " + this.response;
    }

    function isExtra(key) {
    	return ['name', 'message', 'status', 'code',
    	        'response', 'explanation', 'stack'].indexOf(key) < 0;
    }

    // extra properties
    Object.keys(this).filter(isExtra).forEach(function(key) {
    	msg += util.format("\n%s: %s", key, this[key]);
    }, this);

    if (useStack) {
        msg += "\n" + this.stack;
    }
    return msg;
}

    ...

    /*!

    middleware compatible errors, but is too costly. In a 1000 executions
    of toString() it adds ~25% overhead.

    var e = Error();
    Error.captureStackTrace(e);
    if (~e.stack.indexOf("connect/lib/middleware/errorHandler.js")) {
        return this.message;
    }
    */

    // TODO externalization
    var msg = util.format("%s: %s\nCode: %s", this.name, this.message, this.code);
    if (this.explanation) {
        msg += "\nExplanation: " + this.explanation;
    }
    if (this.response) {
        msg += "\nResponse: " + this.response;
    }

    function isExtra(key) {
    	return ['name', 'message', 'status', 'code',
    	        'response', 'explanation', 'stack'].indexOf(key) < 0;
    }

    // extra properties
    Object.keys(this).filter(isExtra).forEach(function(key) {
    	msg += util.format("\n%s: %s", key, this[key]);
    }, this);

    if (useStack) {
        msg += "\n" + this.stack;
    }
    return msg;
}
  • example usage
    ...
```

Create a very barebones error -- you must specify at least the error name:

```js
// barebones
errors.create({name: 'RuntimeError'});
console.log(new errors.RuntimeError().toString());
```

produces:
```
RuntimeError: An unexpected RuntimeError occurred.
Code: 601
```

module errors.Http416Error

function errors.Http416Error (msg, expl, fix)

  • description and source-code
    Http416Error = function (msg, expl, fix) {
	var attrs = {};
	if (typeof msg !== null && typeof msg === 'object') {
		attrs = msg;
		msg = attrs['message'] || defaultMessage;
		if (attrs.hasOwnProperty('stack')
				|| attrs.hasOwnProperty('name')
				|| attrs.hasOwnProperty('code')) {
			throw Error("Properties 'stack', 'name' or 'code' " +
					"cannot be overridden");
		}
	}
	attrs['status'] = attrs['status'] || statusCode;
    msg = msg || defaultMessage;
    expl = expl || defaultExplanation;
    fix = fix || defaultResponse;

    parent.call(this, msg);

    // hack around the defineProperty for stack so
    // we can delay stack formatting until access
    // for performance reasons
    Error.captureStackTrace(stack, scope[className]);

/**
 * Return the stack tracks for the error.
 *
 * @return {String}
 * @api public
 */
    Object.defineProperty(this, 'stack', {
        configurable: true,
        enumerable: false,
        get: function() {
            if (!formattedStack) {
                formattedStack = stack.stack.replace('[object Object]', 'Error: ' + this.message);
            }
            return formattedStack;
        }
    });

/**
 * Return the explanation for this error.
 *
 * @return {String}
 * @api public
*/

    Object.defineProperty(this, 'explanation', {
        value: attrs['explanation'] || expl,
        configurable: true,
        enumerable: true
    });

/**
 * Return the operator response for this error.
 *
 * @return {String}
 * @api public
 */

    Object.defineProperty(this, 'response', {
        value: attrs['response'] || fix,
        configurable: true,
        enumerable: true
    });

/**
 * Return the error code.
 *
 * @return {Number}
 * @api public
 */

    Object.defineProperty(this, 'code', {
        value: attrs['code'] || errorCode,
        configurable: true,
        enumerable: true
    });

/**
 * HTTP status code of this error.
 *
 * If the instance's `code` is not a valid
 * HTTP status code it's normalized to 500.s
 *
 * @return {Number}
 * @api public
 */

    Object.defineProperty(this, 'status', {
        value: attrs['status'] || (http.STATUS_CODES[errorCode] ? errorCode : 500),
        configurable: true,
        // normalize for http status code and connect compat
        enumerable: true
    });

/**
 * Name of this error.
 *
 * @return {String}
 * @api public
 */

    Object.defineProperty(this, 'name', {
        value: className,
        configurable: true,
        enumerable: true
    });

/**
 * Message for this error.
 *
 * @return {String}
 * @api public
 */

    Object.defineProperty(this, 'message', {
        value: attrs['message'] || msg,
        configurable: true,
        enumerable: true
    });

    // expose extra conf attrs as properties
    for (var key in attrs) {
		if (!this.hasOwnProperty(key)) {
			Object.defineProperty(this, key, {
	            value: attrs[key],
	            configurable: true,
	            enumerable: true
	        });
		}
	}

}
  • example usage
    n/a

function errors.Http416Error.prototype.toJSON ()

  • description and source-code
    toJSON = function () {
    // TODO externalization
    return useStack
            ? mixin(this, {stack: this.stack}, true)
            : mixin(this, {}, true);
}
  • example usage
    ...
method.

For example:
```js
errors.stacks(true);
new errors.Http413Error().toString();
// => includes stack trace
new errors.Http413Error().toJSON();
// => includes a 'stack' property
```

You can also use the `errors.stacks()` method without arguments to
retrieve the current value of stacks.

This allows you to write code like:
...

```js
errors.stacks(true);
new errors.Http413Error().toString();
// => includes stack trace
new errors.Http413Error().toJSON();
// => includes a 'stack' property
```

You can also use the `errors.stacks()` method without arguments to
retrieve the current value of stacks.

This allows you to write code like:
...

function errors.Http418Error.prototype.toString ()

  • description and source-code
    toString = function () {

    /*!

    The snippet below would allow us to provide connect errorHandler()
    middleware compatible errors, but is too costly. In a 1000 executions
    of toString() it adds ~25% overhead.

    var e = Error();
    Error.captureStackTrace(e);
    if (~e.stack.indexOf("connect/lib/middleware/errorHandler.js")) {
        return this.message;
    }
    */

    // TODO externalization
    var msg = util.format("%s: %s\nCode: %s", this.name, this.message, this.code);
    if (this.explanation) {
        msg += "\nExplanation: " + this.explanation;
    }
    if (this.response) {
        msg += "\nResponse: " + this.response;
    }

    function isExtra(key) {
    	return ['name', 'message', 'status', 'code',
    	        'response', 'explanation', 'stack'].indexOf(key) < 0;
    }

    // extra properties
    Object.keys(this).filter(isExtra).forEach(function(key) {
    	msg += util.format("\n%s: %s", key, this[key]);
    }, this);

    if (useStack) {
        msg += "\n" + this.stack;
    }
    return msg;
}
  • example usage
    ...
```

Create a very barebones error -- you must specify at least the error name:

```js
// barebones
errors.create({name: 'RuntimeError'});
console.log(new errors.RuntimeError().toString());
```

produces:
```
RuntimeError: An unexpected RuntimeError occurred.
Code: 601
```
...

module errors.Http421Error

function errors.Http421Error (msg, expl, fix)

  • description and source-code
    Http421Error = function (msg, expl, fix) {
	var attrs = {};
	if (typeof msg !== null && typeof msg === 'object') {
		attrs = msg;
		msg = attrs['message'] || defaultMessage;
		if (attrs.hasOwnProperty('stack')
				|| attrs.hasOwnProperty('name')
				|| attrs.hasOwnProperty('code')) {
			throw Error("Properties 'stack', 'name' or 'code' " +
					"cannot be overridden");
		}
	}
	attrs['status'] = attrs['status'] || statusCode;
    msg = msg || defaultMessage;
    expl = expl || defaultExplanation;
    fix = fix || defaultResponse;

    parent.call(this, msg);

    // hack around the defineProperty for stack so
    // we can delay stack formatting until access
    // for performance reasons
    Error.captureStackTrace(stack, scope[className]);

/**
 * Return the stack tracks for the error.
 *
 * @return {String}
 * @api public
 */
    Object.defineProperty(this, 'stack', {
        configurable: true,
        enumerable: false,
        get: function() {
            if (!formattedStack) {
                formattedStack = stack.stack.replace('[object Object]', 'Error: ' + this.message);
            }
            return formattedStack;
        }
    });

/**
 * Return the explanation for this error.
 *
 * @return {String}
 * @api public
*/

    Object.defineProperty(this, 'explanation', {
        value: attrs['explanation'] || expl,
        configurable: true,
        enumerable: true
    });

/**
 * Return the operator response for this error.
 *
 * @return {String}
 * @api public
 */

    Object.defineProperty(this, 'response', {
        value: attrs['response'] || fix,
        configurable: true,
        enumerable: true
    });

/**
 * Return the error code.
 *
 * @return {Number}
 * @api public
 */

    Object.defineProperty(this, 'code', {
        value: attrs['code'] || errorCode,
        configurable: true,
        enumerable: true
    });

/**
 * HTTP status code of this error.
 *
 * If the instance's `code` is not a valid
 * HTTP status code it's normalized to 500.s
 *
 * @return {Number}
 * @api public
 */

    Object.defineProperty(this, 'status', {
        value: attrs['status'] || (http.STATUS_CODES[errorCode] ? errorCode : 500),
        configurable: true,
        // normalize for http status code and connect compat
        enumerable: true
    });

/**
 * Name of this error.
 *
 * @return {String}
 * @api public
 */

    Object.defineProperty(this, 'name', {
        value: className,
        configurable: true,
        enumerable: true
    });

/**
 * Message for this error.
 *
 * @return {String}
 * @api public
 */

    Object.defineProperty(this, 'message', {
        value: attrs['message'] || msg,
        configurable: true,
        enumerable: true
    });

    // expose extra conf attrs as properties
    for (var key in attrs) {
		if (!this.hasOwnProperty(key)) {
			Object.defineProperty(this, key, {
	            value: attrs[key],
	            configurable: true,
	            enumerable: true
	        });
		}
	}

}
  • example usage
    n/a

module errors.Http423Error.prototype

function errors.Http423Error.prototype.toJSON ()

  • description and source-code
    toJSON = function () {
    // TODO externalization
    return useStack
            ? mixin(this, {stack: this.stack}, true)
            : mixin(this, {}, true);
}
  • example usage
    ...
method.

For example:
```js
errors.stacks(true);
new errors.Http413Error().toString();
// => includes stack trace
new errors.Http413Error().toJSON();
// => includes a 'stack' property
```

You can also use the `errors.stacks()` method without arguments to
retrieve the current value of stacks.

This allows you to write code like:
...

function errors.Http423Error.prototype.toString ()

  • description and source-code
    toString = function () {

    /*!

    The snippet below would allow us to provide connect errorHandler()
    middleware compatible errors, but is too costly. In a 1000 executions
    of toString() it adds ~25% overhead.

    var e = Error();
    Error.captureStackTrace(e);
    if (~e.stack.indexOf("connect/lib/middleware/errorHandler.js")) {
        return this.message;
    }
    */

    // TODO externalization
    var msg = util.format("%s: %s\nCode: %s", this.name, this.message, this.code);
    if (this.explanation) {
        msg += "\nExplanation: " + this.explanation;
    }
    if (this.response) {
        msg += "\nResponse: " + this.response;
    }

    function isExtra(key) {
    	return ['name', 'message', 'status', 'code',
    	        'response', 'explanation', 'stack'].indexOf(key) < 0;
    }

    // extra properties
    Object.keys(this).filter(isExtra).forEach(function(key) {
    	msg += util.format("\n%s: %s", key, this[key]);
    }, this);

    if (useStack) {
        msg += "\n" + this.stack;
    }
    return msg;
}
  • example usage
    ...
```

Create a very barebones error -- you must specify at least the error name:

```js
// barebones
errors.create({name: 'RuntimeError'});
console.log(new errors.RuntimeError().toString());
```

produces:
```
RuntimeError: An unexpected RuntimeError occurred.
Code: 601
```

module errors.Http424Error

function errors.Http424Error (msg, expl, fix)

  • description and source-code
    Http424Error = function (msg, expl, fix) {
	var attrs = {};
	if (typeof msg !== null && typeof msg === 'object') {
		attrs = msg;
		msg = attrs['message'] || defaultMessage;
		if (attrs.hasOwnProperty('stack')
				|| attrs.hasOwnProperty('name')
				|| attrs.hasOwnProperty('code')) {
			throw Error("Properties 'stack', 'name' or 'code' " +
					"cannot be overridden");
		}
	}
	attrs['status'] = attrs['status'] || statusCode;
    msg = msg || defaultMessage;
    expl = expl || defaultExplanation;
    fix = fix || defaultResponse;

    parent.call(this, msg);

    // hack around the defineProperty for stack so
    // we can delay stack formatting until access
    // for performance reasons
    Error.captureStackTrace(stack, scope[className]);

/**
 * Return the stack tracks for the error.
 *
 * @return {String}
 * @api public
 */
    Object.defineProperty(this, 'stack', {
        configurable: true,
        enumerable: false,
        get: function() {
            if (!formattedStack) {
                formattedStack = stack.stack.replace('[object Object]', 'Error: ' + this.message);
            }
            return formattedStack;
        }
    });

/**
 * Return the explanation for this error.
 *
 * @return {String}
 * @api public
*/

    Object.defineProperty(this, 'explanation', {
        value: attrs['explanation'] || expl,
        configurable: true,
        enumerable: true
    });

/**
 * Return the operator response for this error.
 *
 * @return {String}
 * @api public
 */

    Object.defineProperty(this, 'response', {
        value: attrs['response'] || fix,
        configurable: true,
        enumerable: true
    });

/**
 * Return the error code.
 *
 * @return {Number}
 * @api public
 */

    Object.defineProperty(this, 'code', {
        value: attrs['code'] || errorCode,
        configurable: true,
        enumerable: true
    });

/**
 * HTTP status code of this error.
 *
 * If the instance's `code` is not a valid
 * HTTP status code it's normalized to 500.s
 *
 * @return {Number}
 * @api public
 */

    Object.defineProperty(this, 'status', {
        value: attrs['status'] || (http.STATUS_CODES[errorCode] ? errorCode : 500),
        configurable: true,
        // normalize for http status code and connect compat
        enumerable: true
    });

/**
 * Name of this error.
 *
 * @return {String}
 * @api public
 */

    Object.defineProperty(this, 'name', {
        value: className,
        configurable: true,
        enumerable: true
    });

/**
 * Message for this error.
 *
 * @return {String}
 * @api public
 */

    Object.defineProperty(this, 'message', {
        value: attrs['message'] || msg,
        configurable: true,
        enumerable: true
    });

    // expose extra conf attrs as properties
    for (var key in attrs) {
		if (!this.hasOwnProperty(key)) {
			Object.defineProperty(this, key, {
	            value: attrs[key],
	            configurable: true,
	            enumerable: true
	        });
		}
	}

}
  • example usage
    ...

For example:
```js
errors.mapper('RangeError', function(rangeError) {
    return new errors.Http412Error('Invalid range requested');
})
.mapper('ReferenceError', function(refError) {
    return new errors.Http424Error('Bad reference given');
})
.mapper('SyntaxError', function(syntaxError) {
    return new errors.Http400Error('Invalid syntax');
});

 * @return {String}
 * @api public
 */

    Object.defineProperty(this, 'name', {
        value: className,
        configurable: true,
        enumerable: true
    });

/**
 * Message for this error.
 *
 * @return {String}
 * @api public
 */

    Object.defineProperty(this, 'message', {
        value: attrs['message'] || msg,
        configurable: true,
        enumerable: true
    });

    // expose extra conf attrs as properties
    for (var key in attrs) {
		if (!this.hasOwnProperty(key)) {
			Object.defineProperty(this, key, {
	            value: attrs[key],
	            configurable: true,
	            enumerable: true
	        });
		}
	}

module errors.Http426Error.prototype

function errors.Http426Error.prototype.toJSON ()

  • description and source-code
    toJSON = function () {
    // TODO externalization
    return useStack
            ? mixin(this, {stack: this.stack}, true)
            : mixin(this, {}, true);
}
  • example usage
    ...
method.

For example:
```js
errors.stacks(true);
new errors.Http413Error().toString();
// => includes stack trace
new errors.Http413Error().toJSON();
// => includes a 'stack' property
```

You can also use the `errors.stacks()` method without arguments to
retrieve the current value of stacks.

This allows you to write code like:
...

function errors.Http426Error.prototype.toString ()

  • description and source-code
    toString = function () {

    /*!

    The snippet below would allow us to provide connect errorHandler()
    middleware compatible errors, but is too costly. In a 1000 executions
    of toString() it adds ~25% overhead.

    var e = Error();
    Error.captureStackTrace(e);
    if (~e.stack.indexOf("connect/lib/middleware/errorHandler.js")) {
        return this.message;
    }
    */

    // TODO externalization
    var msg = util.format("%s: %s\nCode: %s", this.name, this.message, this.code);
    if (this.explanation) {
        msg += "\nExplanation: " + this.explanation;
    }
    if (this.response) {
        msg += "\nResponse: " + this.response;
    }

    function isExtra(key) {
    	return ['name', 'message', 'status', 'code',
    	        'response', 'explanation', 'stack'].indexOf(key) < 0;
    }

    // extra properties
    Object.keys(this).filter(isExtra).forEach(function(key) {
    	msg += util.format("\n%s: %s", key, this[key]);
    }, this);

    if (useStack) {
        msg += "\n" + this.stack;
    }
    return msg;
}
  • example usage
    ...
```

Create a very barebones error -- you must specify at least the error name:

```js
// barebones
errors.create({name: 'RuntimeError'});
console.log(new errors.RuntimeError().toString());
```

produces:
```
RuntimeError: An unexpected RuntimeError occurred.
Code: 601
```

module errors.Http428Error

function errors.Http428Error (msg, expl, fix)

  • description and source-code
    Http428Error = function (msg, expl, fix) {
	var attrs = {};
	if (typeof msg !== null && typeof msg === 'object') {
		attrs = msg;
		msg = attrs['message'] || defaultMessage;
		if (attrs.hasOwnProperty('stack')
				|| attrs.hasOwnProperty('name')
				|| attrs.hasOwnProperty('code')) {
			throw Error("Properties 'stack', 'name' or 'code' " +
					"cannot be overridden");
		}
	}
	attrs['status'] = attrs['status'] || statusCode;
    msg = msg || defaultMessage;
    expl = expl || defaultExplanation;
    fix = fix || defaultResponse;

    parent.call(this, msg);

    // hack around the defineProperty for stack so
    // we can delay stack formatting until access
    // for performance reasons
    Error.captureStackTrace(stack, scope[className]);

/**
 * Return the stack tracks for the error.
 *
 * @return {String}
 * @api public
 */
    Object.defineProperty(this, 'stack', {
        configurable: true,
        enumerable: false,
        get: function() {
            if (!formattedStack) {
                formattedStack = stack.stack.replace('[object Object]', 'Error: ' + this.message);
            }
            return formattedStack;
        }
    });

/**
 * Return the explanation for this error.
 *
 * @return {String}
 * @api public
*/

    Object.defineProperty(this, 'explanation', {
        value: attrs['explanation'] || expl,
        configurable: true,
        enumerable: true
    });

/**
 * Return the operator response for this error.
 *
 * @return {String}
 * @api public
 */

    Object.defineProperty(this, 'response', {
        value: attrs['response'] || fix,
        configurable: true,
        enumerable: true
    });

/**
 * Return the error code.
 *
 * @return {Number}
 * @api public
 */

    Object.defineProperty(this, 'code', {
        value: attrs['code'] || errorCode,
        configurable: true,
        enumerable: true
    });

/**
 * HTTP status code of this error.
 *
 * If the instance's `code` is not a valid
 * HTTP status code it's normalized to 500.s
 *
 * @return {Number}
 * @api public
 */

    Object.defineProperty(this, 'status', {
        value: attrs['status'] || (http.STATUS_CODES[errorCode] ? errorCode : 500),
        configurable: true,
        // normalize for http status code and connect compat
        enumerable: true
    });

/**
 * Name of this error.
 *
 * @return {String}
 * @api public
 */

    Object.defineProperty(this, 'name', {
        value: className,
        configurable: true,
        enumerable: true
    });

/**
 * Message for this error.
 *
 * @return {String}
 * @api public
 */

    Object.defineProperty(this, 'message', {
        value: attrs['message'] || msg,
        configurable: true,
        enumerable: true
    });

    // expose extra conf attrs as properties
    for (var key in attrs) {
		if (!this.hasOwnProperty(key)) {
			Object.defineProperty(this, key, {
	            value: attrs[key],
	            configurable: true,
	            enumerable: true
	        });
		}
	}

}
  • example usage
    n/a

 * If the instance's `code` is not a valid
 * HTTP status code it's normalized to 500.s
 *
 * @return {Number}
 * @api public
 */

    Object.defineProperty(this, 'status', {
        value: attrs['status'] || (http.STATUS_CODES[errorCode] ? errorCode : 500),
        configurable: true,
        // normalize for http status code and connect compat
        enumerable: true
    });

/**
 * Name of this error.
 *
 * @return {String}
 * @api public
 */

    Object.defineProperty(this, 'name', {
        value: className,
        configurable: true,
        enumerable: true
    });

/**
 * Message for this error.
 *
 * @return {String}
 * @api public
 */

    Object.defineProperty(this, 'message', {
        value: attrs['message'] || msg,
        configurable: true,
        enumerable: true
    });

    // expose extra conf attrs as properties
    for (var key in attrs) {
		if (!this.hasOwnProperty(key)) {
			Object.defineProperty(this, key, {
	            value: attrs[key],
	            configurable: true,
	            enumerable: true
	        });
		}
	}

}

module errors.Http431Error.prototype

function errors.Http431Error.prototype.toJSON ()

  • description and source-code
    toJSON = function () {
    // TODO externalization
    return useStack
            ? mixin(this, {stack: this.stack}, true)
            : mixin(this, {}, true);
}
  • example usage
    ...
method.

For example:
```js
errors.stacks(true);
new errors.Http413Error().toString();
// => includes stack trace
new errors.Http413Error().toJSON();
// => includes a 'stack' property
```

You can also use the `errors.stacks()` method without arguments to
retrieve the current value of stacks.

This allows you to write code like:
...

function errors.Http431Error.prototype.toString ()

  • description and source-code
    toString = function () {

    /*!

    The snippet below would allow us to provide connect errorHandler()
    middleware compatible errors, but is too costly. In a 1000 executions
    of toString() it adds ~25% overhead.

    var e = Error();
    Error.captureStackTrace(e);
    if (~e.stack.indexOf("connect/lib/middleware/errorHandler.js")) {
        return this.message;
    }
    */

    // TODO externalization
    var msg = util.format("%s: %s\nCode: %s", this.name, this.message, this.code);
    if (this.explanation) {
        msg += "\nExplanation: " + this.explanation;
    }
    if (this.response) {
        msg += "\nResponse: " + this.response;
    }

    function isExtra(key) {
    	return ['name', 'message', 'status', 'code',
    	        'response', 'explanation', 'stack'].indexOf(key) < 0;
    }

    // extra properties
    Object.keys(this).filter(isExtra).forEach(function(key) {
    	msg += util.format("\n%s: %s", key, this[key]);
    }, this);

    if (useStack) {
        msg += "\n" + this.stack;
    }
    return msg;
}
  • example usage
    ...
```

Create a very barebones error -- you must specify at least the error name:

```js
// barebones
errors.create({name: 'RuntimeError'});
console.log(new errors.RuntimeError().toString());
```

produces:
```
RuntimeError: An unexpected RuntimeError occurred.
Code: 601
```

module errors.Http451Error

function errors.Http451Error (msg, expl, fix)

  • description and source-code
    Http451Error = function (msg, expl, fix) {
	var attrs = {};
	if (typeof msg !== null && typeof msg === 'object') {
		attrs = msg;
		msg = attrs['message'] || defaultMessage;
		if (attrs.hasOwnProperty('stack')
				|| attrs.hasOwnProperty('name')
				|| attrs.hasOwnProperty('code')) {
			throw Error("Properties 'stack', 'name' or 'code' " +
					"cannot be overridden");
		}
	}
	attrs['status'] = attrs['status'] || statusCode;
    msg = msg || defaultMessage;
    expl = expl || defaultExplanation;
    fix = fix || defaultResponse;

    parent.call(this, msg);

    // hack around the defineProperty for stack so
    // we can delay stack formatting until access
    // for performance reasons
    Error.captureStackTrace(stack, scope[className]);

/**
 * Return the stack tracks for the error.
 *
 * @return {String}
 * @api public
 */
    Object.defineProperty(this, 'stack', {
        configurable: true,
        enumerable: false,
        get: function() {
            if (!formattedStack) {
                formattedStack = stack.stack.replace('[object Object]', 'Error: ' + this.message);
            }
            return formattedStack;
        }
    });

/**
 * Return the explanation for this error.
 *
 * @return {String}
 * @api public
*/

    Object.defineProperty(this, 'explanation', {
        value: attrs['explanation'] || expl,
        configurable: true,
        enumerable: true
    });

/**
 * Return the operator response for this error.
 *
 * @return {String}
 * @api public
 */

    Object.defineProperty(this, 'response', {
        value: attrs['response'] || fix,
        configurable: true,
        enumerable: true
    });

/**
 * Return the error code.
 *
 * @return {Number}
 * @api public
 */

    Object.defineProperty(this, 'code', {
        value: attrs['code'] || errorCode,
        configurable: true,
        enumerable: true
    });

/**
 * HTTP status code of this error.
 *
 * If the instance's `code` is not a valid
 * HTTP status code it's normalized to 500.s
 *
 * @return {Number}
 * @api public
 */

    Object.defineProperty(this, 'status', {
        value: attrs['status'] || (http.STATUS_CODES[errorCode] ? errorCode : 500),
        configurable: true,
        // normalize for http status code and connect compat
        enumerable: true
    });

/**
 * Name of this error.
 *
 * @return {String}
 * @api public
 */

    Object.defineProperty(this, 'name', {
        value: className,
        configurable: true,
        enumerable: true
    });

/**
 * Message for this error.
 *
 * @return {String}
 * @api public
 */

    Object.defineProperty(this, 'message', {
        value: attrs['message'] || msg,
        configurable: true,
        enumerable: true
    });

    // expose extra conf attrs as properties
    for (var key in attrs) {
		if (!this.hasOwnProperty(key)) {
			Object.defineProperty(this, key, {
	            value: attrs[key],
	            configurable: true,
	            enumerable: true
	        });
		}
	}

}

  • example usage
    ...
naming convention `Http[code]Error`. For example `Http401Error` and
`Http500Error` which have a code of `401` and `500` respectively.

For example to leverage the HTTP errors:
```js
throw new errors.Http401Error();
// ...
throw new errors.Http500Error('Something bad happened');
```

## Connect/Express middleware integration

**Compatibility**
Errors version 0.1.0 only works with Express < 4.0.0.

 * Return the explanation for this error.
 *
 * @return {String}
 * @api public
*/

    Object.defineProperty(this, 'explanation', {
        value: attrs['explanation'] || expl,
        configurable: true,
        enumerable: true
    });

/**
 * Return the operator response for this error.
 *
 * @return {String}
 * @api public
 */

    Object.defineProperty(this, 'response', {
        value: attrs['response'] || fix,
        configurable: true,
        enumerable: true
    });

/**
 * Return the error code.
 *
 * @return {Number}
 * @api public
 */

    Object.defineProperty(this, 'code', {
        value: attrs['code'] || errorCode,
        configurable: true,
        enumerable: true
    });

/**
 * HTTP status code of this error.
 *
 * If the instance's `code` is not a valid
 * HTTP status code it's normalized to 500.s
 *
 * @return {Number}
 * @api public
 */

    Object.defineProperty(this, 'status', {
        value: attrs['status'] || (http.STATUS_CODES[errorCode] ? errorCode : 500),
        configurable: true,
        // normalize for http status code and connect compat
        enumerable: true
    });

/**
 * Name of this error.
 *
 * @return {String}
 * @api public
 */

    Object.defineProperty(this, 'name', {
        value: className,
        configurable: true,
        enumerable: true
    });

/**
 * Message for this error.
 *
 * @return {String}
 * @api public
 */

    Object.defineProperty(this, 'message', {
        value: attrs['message'] || msg,
        configurable: true,
        enumerable: true
    });

    // expose extra conf attrs as properties
    for (var key in attrs) {
		if (!this.hasOwnProperty(key)) {
			Object.defineProperty(this, key, {
	            value: attrs[key],
	            configurable: true,
	            enumerable: true
	        });
		}
	}

}
